| 0:51:10| Okay, thank you. So, I will go ahead and read the resolution. It's the resolution for the| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3070)|
| 0:51:17| Commission of Knox County, Tennessee recognizing and honoring Black History Month. Okay. The| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3077)|
| 0:51:27| birthdays of President Abraham Lincoln and abolitionist Frederick Douglass inspired the| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3087)|
| 0:51:32| creation of Negro History Week, the precursor to Black History Month. And whereas the month| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3092)|
| 0:51:38| of February is officially celebrated as Black History Month, which dates to 1926, when Carter| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3098)|
| 0:51:45| G. Woodson set aside a special period of time in February to recognize the heritage and| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3105)|
| 0:51:51| achievement of Black Americans. Since the inception of the Association for the Study| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3111)|
| 0:51:57| of African American Life and History, the founder, Carter G. Woodson, stressed the importance| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3117)|
| 0:52:02| of providing a theme each year to Black History Month to focus on the attention of the public.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3122)|
| 0:52:09| And whereas the 2021 theme for Black History Month is the Black Family, Representation,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3129)|
| 0:52:15| Identity, and Diversity. And whereas the Black Family has been a topic of study in many disciplines,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3135)|
| 0:52:22| history, literature, visual arts, and film studies, sociology, anthropology, and social| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3142)|
| 0:52:29| policy, making it a unifying theme for celebration in 2021. And whereas the Black Family has| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3149)|
| 0:52:36| been reverent, stereotyped, and vilified from the days of slavery until now. Whereas it| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3156)|
| 0:52:41| is appropriate for the people of Knox County to continue to educate, reflect, respect,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3161)|
| 0:52:48| cherish, and sustain the contributions of Black Americans on a local, national, international| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3168)|
| 0:52:53| level. Now, therefore, it be resolved by the Commission of Knox County as follows. The| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3173)|
| 0:52:59| Knox County Commission hereby recognizes and honors the month of February as Black History| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3179)|
| 0:53:05| Month in Knox County, and encourages all citizens to celebrate the past and current achievements| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3185)|
| 0:53:12| and contributions of African Americans have made to our nation. Be it further resolved that the| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3192)|
| 0:53:17| Knox County Commission expresses its desire to continue to be a legislative body that is| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3197)|
| 0:53:24| intentional in its support of policies that create diversity, equity, and inclusion. Be it further| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3204)|
| 0:53:32| resolved that this resolution to take effect from after its passage as provided by the Charter of| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3212)|

| 1:00:05| Thank you, Commissioner and members of the County Commission. My name is Julie Gautreaux. I live at| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3605)|
| 1:00:10| 313 Woodland Trace Drive in Farragut. I understand that the proposed inmate calling solutions| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3610)|
| 1:00:18| contract is on consent tonight, but I want to make the commission and the public aware of some| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3618)|
| 1:00:23| local history around this issue. I've been a public defender for 30 years, and I remember when| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3623)|
| 1:00:30| the Roger D. Williams Detention Facility was built back in 92. It was designed for in-person| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3630)|
| 1:00:36| visitation for prisoners and their families. Millions of county dollars were spent on its| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3636)|
| 1:00:42| construction. In 2014, Sheriff Jones proposed a contract with Securus Technologies to install| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3642)|
| 1:00:49| video visitation and other tech services, and that made sense. Times are changing. New technology| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3649)|
| 1:00:55| presents new methods of communication. It's a great option for folks who can't visit.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3655)|
| 1:01:01| But after the commission approved that contract, the sheriff eliminated the in-person option| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3661)|
| 1:01:07| that the Roger D. Williams facility was designed for. Every so-called security-based justification| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3667)|
| 1:01:16| for this policy has been debunked by their own records that were obtained via open records in| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3676)|
| 1:01:22| 2018. The reason for the termination of in-person was financial incentive. Incarcerated people or| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3682)|
| 1:01:30| their families have to pay for remote visitation. The tech was installed at no cost to the county.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3690)|
| 1:01:36| The sheriff didn't have the hassle of staffing on-site visitation, and the county got a 50| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3696)|
| 1:01:41| percent commission off the monies being paid to Securus by the families. Now Sheriff Spangler| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3701)|
| 1:01:48| has presented a deal with ICS with an even better percentage. I understand it's 88 percent.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=3708)|

| 2:39:29| the Commission of Knox County, Tennessee, recognizing and honoring Black History Month.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9569)|
| 2:39:35| Okay. The birthdays of President Abraham Lincoln and abolitionist Frederick Douglass inspired the| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9575)|
| 2:39:43| creation of Negro History Week, the precursor to Black History Month. And whereas the month| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9583)|
| 2:39:50| of February is officially celebrated as Black History Month, which dates to 1926, when Carter| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9590)|
| 2:39:57| G. Woodson set aside a special period of time in February to recognize the heritage and achievement| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9597)|
| 2:40:04| of Black Americans. Since the inception of the Association for the Study of African American Life| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9604)|
| 2:40:10| and History, the founder, Carter G. Woodson, stressed the importance of providing a theme| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9610)|
| 2:40:16| each year to Black History Month to focus on the attention of the public. And whereas the 2021| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9616)|
| 2:40:23| theme for Black History Month is the Black Family, Representation, Identity, and Diversity.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9623)|
| 2:40:29| And whereas the Black Family has been a topic of study in many disciplines, history, literature,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9629)|
| 2:40:37| visual arts, and film studies, sociology, anthropology, and social policy, making it a| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9637)|
| 2:40:42| unifying theme for celebration in 2021. And whereas the Black Family has been reverent,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9642)|
| 2:40:48| stereotyped, and vilified from the days of slavery until now. Whereas it is appropriate for the| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9648)|
| 2:40:55| people of Knox County to continue to educate, reflect, respect, cherish, and sustain the| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9655)|
| 2:41:01| contributions of Black Americans on a local, national, international level. Now, therefore,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9661)|
| 2:41:07| it be resolved by the Commission of Knox County as follows. The Knox County Commission hereby| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9667)|
| 2:41:13| recognizes and honors the month of February as Black History Month in Knox County and encourages| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9673)|
| 2:41:19| all citizens to celebrate the past and current achievements and contributions of African Americans| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9679)|
| 2:41:26| have made to our nation. Be it further resolved that the Knox County Commission expresses its| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9686)|
| 2:41:32| desire to continue to be a legislative body that is intentional in its support of policies that| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9692)|
| 2:41:40| create diversity, equity, and inclusion. Be it further resolved that this resolution to take| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9700)|
| 2:41:45| effect from after its passage as provided by the Charter of Knox County, Tennessee,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/co-com-r-267-210222?start=9705)|
